**GT:** `0.1728*(1 - P/48.55)*P + 0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*(-0.924 + P)))`

- First term: `0.1728*P - 0.003559*P²` (a linear + quadratic in P)
- Second term: `0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*P + 1.408))` (a sigmoidal term in P)

Key observations about GT:
1. GT depends only on P, NOT on t
2. GT has: P² term, P term, and a sigmoidal term `P/(1 + exp(linear in P))`
3. The sigmoidal term `P/(1+exp(a+bP))` is NOT a simple polynomial, exponential, or trigonometric function

For candidates with `t` dependence: we need to be able to set all `t`-dependent terms to zero (by setting their coefficients to 0).

Let me check which candidates can, after zeroing t-dependent terms, match the GT structure.

**GT (t-independent form):** `c0*P² + c1*P + f(P)` where `f(P) = 0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*P + 1.408))`

The sigmoidal term `P/(1+exp(a+bP))` can be rewritten. Note that `1/(1+exp(-x)) = sigmoid(x)`, so this is `P * sigmoid(1.524*P - 1.408)`.

Now I need to check: can any candidate's non-t-dependent terms produce this sigmoid-like function?

**Key functional forms that CANNOT match the sigmoid:**
- Polynomials in P
- `exp(P*c)` alone (not a sigmoid)
- `sin(...)` terms
- `P^c` power terms
- `P/(P+c)` rational functions (this is NOT a sigmoid)

**What CAN match:** `exp(P*c)` combined with other terms in specific ways, or explicit sigmoid-like structures.

Let me check candidates with `exp(P*...)` terms:

For the sigmoid `P/(1+exp(a+bP))`, we can write it as `P*exp(-a-bP)/(1+exp(-a-bP))` or note that `P/(1+exp(f(P)))` is NOT simply `c*exp(P*d)`.

Actually, `P/(1+exp(g))` where g is linear in P — can this be expressed as `P² + P + c*exp(P*d)`? No, because `exp(P*d)` grows/decays exponentially while the sigmoid saturates.

Let me systematically check candidates that have `exp(P*...)` type terms after zeroing t:

**Candidates 4, 7, 14, etc.** with `exp(P^c * d)`: Setting c6=1 gives `exp(c*P)`, which is a pure exponential, not a sigmoid.

After zeroing t terms (set c5=0): `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2/(P*c3 + 1)`
This is rational in P: `P²*c0 + P*c1 + c2*P/(c3*P + 1)`. This is NOT a sigmoid.

**Candidate 42:** Similar rational structure, not sigmoid.

None of these candidates contain the structure `P/(1 + exp(linear in P))`. The sigmoid function cannot be represented by polynomials, rational functions, simple exponentials, power functions, or trigonometric functions.
